                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 3<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=smll202412449-fig-0003&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fsmll.202412449" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">CV curves of Fe<sub>x</sub>Co<sub>3-x</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs electrode within a) 0.01–3&nbsp;V at a scan rate of 0.1&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup>. Galvanostatic charge/discharge profiles of the Fe<sub>x</sub>Co<sub>3-x</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs electrode at a current density of 500&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> within b) 0.01–3&nbsp;V. c) Cycling performance of Fe<sub>x</sub>Co<sub>3-x</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs and Co<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs electrode at 500&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> within 0.01–3&nbsp;V. d) Rate performance of Fe<sub>x</sub>Co<sub>3-x</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs and Co<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs electrode. e) The cycling life of Fe<sub>x</sub>Co<sub>3-x</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs and Co<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs with different current densities, the capacity retention is &lt;50%. f) Comparison of performance data with other anode materials for SIBs reported in recent literature.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            <p>In the CV curves of the Fe<sub>x</sub>Co<sub>3-x</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs electrode in the potential window of 0.01-3&nbsp;V, there are several reduction peaks at 0.60 and 0.20&nbsp;V in the first reduction scan, which correspond to the oxidation peak at ≈1.60 and 2.10&nbsp;V, respectively.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202412449-bib-0001" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202412449-bib-0001_R_d3386538e1700" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 1 - Chem. Eng. J.">1</a>, <a href="#smll202412449-bib-0050" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202412449-bib-0050_R_d3386538e1700" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 50 - RSC Adv.">50</a>, <a href="#smll202412449-bib-0051" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202412449-bib-0051_R_d3386538e1700" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 51 - J. Mater. Chem. A">51</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> These redox peaks are attributed to the multiple-step intercalation of Na<sup>+</sup> into Fe<sub>x</sub>Co<sub>3-x</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs and subsequent conversion reactions. The corresponding phase transition reaction process can be observed in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S7</a> (Supporting Information). Interestingly, the discharge-specific capacity of the Fe<sub>x</sub>Co<sub>3-x</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs electrode increases slowly to a very high capacity and then can remain stable after many cycles. As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202412449-fig-0003">3b</a>, the charge curves of each cycle nearly overlap in the section of 0.01–0.60&nbsp;V, but the curves gradually become a wider plateau at ≈0.60 and 1.20&nbsp;V with the increase of cycle number, indicating at this voltage the main electrochemical conversion reactions are taking place. It is worth mentioning that the cobalt oxide (CoO) often undergoes the reversible conversion reaction between Co and Fe<sub>x</sub>Co<sub>3-x</sub>O<sub>4</sub>, which can be confirmed from ex situ XRD (<b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#smll202412449-fig-0004">4a</a>) and in situ Raman (Figure <a href="#smll202412449-fig-0004">4b</a>). Therefore, the high-oxidation end product after recharge to 3.0&nbsp;V indicates the enhanced kinetics of conversion reactions for the as-prepared electrodes. The conversion reactions agreed well with the galvanostatic charge–discharge curves. Compared with the increasing cycle of discharge profiles, two sloping plateaus gradually emerge ≈1.60 and 0.80&nbsp;V. Furthermore, the charge and discharge curves have the same shape in the range of 0.01–3&nbsp;V, indicating that a strong reversibility of the conversion reaction. It is worth mentioning that a similar redox couple can be observed in the CV curves of the pure Co<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs electrode (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S8</a>, Supporting Information), indicating this is a common electrochemical side reaction in Co-based oxide.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202412449-bib-0001" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202412449-bib-0001_R_d3386538e1751" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 1 - Chem. Eng. J.">1</a>, <a href="#smll202412449-bib-0016" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202412449-bib-0016_R_d3386538e1751" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 16 - Appl. Sci.-Basel">16</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The following chapter will provide an in-depth analysis of the conversion reactions, utilizing both in situ Raman and ex situ XRD.</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="smll202412449-fig-0004"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/892ce000-7308-4c1c-98a1-9c0ade2a964d/smll202412449-fig-0004-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/892ce000-7308-4c1c-98a1-9c0ade2a964d/smll202412449-fig-0004-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/0d64e5d3-3de5-4566-9d93-9610d4e5b62e/smll202412449-fig-0004-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/892ce000-7308-4c1c-98a1-9c0ade2a964d/smll202412449-fig-0004-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 4<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=smll202412449-fig-0004&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fsmll.202412449" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Reaction mechanism investigation of Fe<sub>x</sub>Co<sub>3-x</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs electrode for SIB a) ex situ XRD patterns at various potential states. b) in situ Raman spectra of Fe<sub>x</sub>Co<sub>3-x</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs. c) the contour of the Fe<sub>x</sub>Co<sub>3-x</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs electrode at different scan rates. d) ln(<i>i</i>)–ln(<i>v</i>) curves (b-value determination). e) Contribution ratios of the surface process in the Fe<sub>x</sub>Co<sub>3-x</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs electrode at different scan rates. (f) DRT analysis based on the in situ GEIS of Fe<sub>x</sub>Co<sub>3-x</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            <p>The Fe<sub>x</sub>Co<sub>3-x</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs show excellent cycle performance in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202412449-fig-0003">3c</a>. The typical charge/discharge curves of the Fe<sub>x</sub>Co<sub>3-x</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs electrode for the first cycles at 500&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> exhibited a high initial discharge/charge capacity of 949.6/820.8&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> with a remarkable initial Coulombic efficiency (ICE) of 86.4% within the voltage range of 0.01–3&nbsp;V. The irreversible capacity loss is due to the formation of a solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) layer. The Fe<sub>x</sub>Co<sub>3-x</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs electrode exhibits outstanding cycling stability, maintaining a high specific capacity of 786.2&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g−¹ even after 500 cycles at 500&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−</sup>¹. The coulombic efficiency of the Fe<sub>x</sub>Co<sub>3-x</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs electrode is around 100% (500&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>) at the fewest charge/discharge cycles, thus reflecting the rapid construction of the stability SEI film. Noticeably, the reversible capacity of Fe<sub>x</sub>Co<sub>3-x</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs is higher than that of the theoretical capacity of 890&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> with 6 Na<sup>+</sup> storing.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202412449-bib-0022" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202412449-bib-0022_R_d3386538e1864" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 22 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">22</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The excess reversible capacity might be ascribed to synergistic effects with the supper P. The reversible capacity contribution of the conductive additive supper P is 164.8 mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> within 0.01-3&nbsp;V.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202412449-bib-0052" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202412449-bib-0052_R_d3386538e1871" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 52 - Adv. Energy Mater.">52</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> To further investigate the rate performance of Fe<sub>x</sub>Co<sub>3-x</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs, they were conducted at various current densities. The corresponding 5th discharge capacities of the electrode were 916.2, 667.8, 552.3, 458.6, and 402.9&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, with the current densities gradually increasing to 0.2, 0.5, 1, 2, and 3&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> within the voltage range of 0.01–3&nbsp;V, respectively (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202412449-fig-0003">3d</a>). It is worth mentioning that an unexpected specific capacity of 402.9&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> can be achieved at a high current density of 3.0&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. Fe<sub>x</sub>Co<sub>3-x</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs exhibited a stable performance for 150 cycles at a current density of 3.0 A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> as shown in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S20</a> (Supporting Information). It is especially noteworthy that the high-rate response at 3.0 A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> means an ultrafast charge/discharge time of &lt;15&nbsp;min, highlighting the high-rate application of the Fe<sub>x</sub>Co<sub>3-x</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs electrode in SIBs. Furthermore, the current density returned to 500&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, and the capacity of Fe<sub>x</sub>Co<sub>3-x</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs can also reach 592.8&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, which demonstrated excellent reversibility and superior stability of the Fe<sub>x</sub>Co<sub>3-x</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs anode electrode toward SIBs. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202412449-fig-0003">3e</a> presents the number of cycles recorded at different charge/discharge currents. A representative cycling curve at a current density of 2.0&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−</sup>¹ is presented in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S21</a> (Supporting Information). As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202412449-fig-0003">3e</a>, the Fe<sub>x</sub>Co<sub>3-x</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs electrode demonstrates a remarkable cycle life, maintaining its capacity over an extended number of cycles, thereby indicating its potential for long-term stability and reliability in battery applications. Compared with the cobalt oxide anode reported in recent years (Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S8</a>, Supporting Information), which includes the capacities, rate capabilities, ICE, cycling performance, and voltage window, it is clear that the rate performance of the Fe<sub>x</sub>Co<sub>3-x</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs electrode is the best among the reported cobalt oxide anode materials in SIBs (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202412449-fig-0003">3f</a>).</p>
            </section>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smll202412449-sec-0050">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="smll202412449-sec-0050-title">2.3 Kinetics and Reaction Mechanism</h3>
            
            <p>We further explored the origin of the superior rate performance in the Fe<sub>x</sub>Co<sub>3-x</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs electrode and investigated the kinetics characterization by electrochemical characterization techniques (Figure <a href="#smll202412449-fig-0004">4</a>). To reveal the Na<sup>+</sup> storage mechanism and the formation of excellent rate performance of Fe<sub>x</sub>Co<sub>3-x</sub>O<sub>4</sub>, the post-treatment electrode was investigated based on ex situ XRD, in situ Raman, and in situ galvanostatic electrochemical impedance spectra (in situ GEIS) at various depths of the second discharge/charge. The selected XRD patterns of the Fe<sub>x</sub>Co<sub>3-x</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs at various potential states (including open circuit voltage [OCV]) were performed during the first cycle at 100&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, as depicted in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202412449-fig-0004">4a</a>. In the ex situ XRD analysis, characteristic XRD peaks for the Na<sub>2</sub>O crystal phase were observed at voltages of 1.80, 0.60, 0.20, and 1.20&nbsp;V. Similarly, distinct signal peaks corresponding to Co were detected at 0.60, 0.20, 0.80, 1.20, and 2.10&nbsp;V. This is consistent with the results of the reaction equations mentioned in Chapter II.</p>
            
            <p>Cyclic Voltammetry (CV) measurements of Fe<sub>x</sub>Co<sub>3-x</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs electrodes are performed at scan rates from 0.2 to 1&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup>. As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202412449-fig-0004">4c</a> and Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S9a</a> (Supporting Information), by converting the CV curve into a contour plot, the position of the oxidation and reduction peaks can be clearly. The contour plot was derived from the CV curve at different scanning rates provide a more detailed visualization of peak position shifts (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S15</a>, Supporting Information). Interestingly, cathodic and anodic scans were able to observe the oxidation peak at 1.75&nbsp;V and the reduction peak at 0.75&nbsp;V respectively, which agrees well with the Na<sup>+</sup> conversion reaction of the galvanostatic charge/discharge profile in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202412449-fig-0003">3b</a>, with an obvious distinct plateau area. As we know, according to the relationship between peak currents (<i>i</i>) and scan rates (<i>v</i>) (Equations <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1</a> and <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S2</a>, Supporting Information), we can obtain the <i>b</i> value.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202412449-bib-0001" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202412449-bib-0001_R_d3386538e2043" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 1 - Chem. Eng. J.">1</a>, <a href="#smll202412449-bib-0053" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202412449-bib-0053_R_d3386538e2043" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 53 - Eng. Sci.">53</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In general, values of <i>b</i> close to 0.5 indicate a diffusion-controlled process, whereas values of <i>b</i> approaching 1.0 represent a capacitive process. As depicted in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202412449-fig-0004">4d</a>, both display the fitted slope <i>b</i>-values of ≈0.5 for Fe<sub>x</sub>Co<sub>3-x</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs electrodes, suggesting that the electrochemical process is dominated by a combination of surfaced-controlled pseudocapacitive and diffusion-controlled behavior for Na-ion storage. For anode material surface control, pseudocapacitive can provide high capacity. Moreover, the quantification of the capacity contribution ratio can be further calculated from Equation <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S3</a> (Supporting Information). As results, the capacitive contribution ratio of the Fe<sub>x</sub>Co<sub>3-x</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs electrode gradually increases from 26% to 57% (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202412449-fig-0004">4e</a>) for an electrode. The detailed of the kinetic analysis are displayed in Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S5</a> (Supporting Information). The Fe<sub>x</sub>Co<sub>3-x</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs electrode shows a higher diffusion contribution ratio at the same scan rate than the Co<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub> electrode (Figures <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S9b</a> and <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S15b</a>, Supporting Information) in the sodiation process, which suggests that sodium ion diffusion plays a critical role in determining the electrochemical properties of the Fe<sub>x</sub>Co<sub>3-x</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs. At a scan rate of 0.6&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup>, the contour of the pseudocapacitance contribution is closely aligned with the CV curve in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S10</a> (Supporting Information), confirming the validity of the pseudocapacitance fitting. The kinetics of Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion coefficient (D<sub>Na</sub><sup>+</sup>) of the Fe<sub>x</sub>Co<sub>3-x</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs electrode is also investigated by CV at various scan rates (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S15a</a>, Supporting Information) and calculated using the Randles–Sevcik equation (Equation <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S4</a>, Supporting Information). According to the linear fitting results of I<sub>p</sub> and v<sup>1/2</sup> (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S11</a>, Supporting Information), the D<sub>Na</sub><sup>+</sup> of the Fe<sub>x</sub>Co<sub>3-x</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs electrode is estimated to be 7.68&nbsp;×&nbsp;10<sup>−12</sup> cm<sup>2</sup>&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup>, which is two orders of magnitude greater than that of Co<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub> (6.59&nbsp;×&nbsp;10<sup>−14</sup>&nbsp;cm<sup>2</sup>&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup>) electrodes. This result is highly consistent with the sodium ion diffusion coefficients obtained from the GITT test (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S12</a>, Supporting Information), demonstrating comparable magnitudes and reinforcing the reliability of the measurements across both methods. Note that the electrochemical performance of anode materials in SIBs depended on the competition between adsorption and diffusion of ions on the host. Therefore, the high Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion coefficient of the Fe<sub>x</sub>Co<sub>3-x</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs electrode will boost the electrochemical performance for sodium ion storage.</p>
            
            <p>Electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (EIS, Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S13</a>, Supporting Information) was performed to better understand the effect of Fe doping on its kinetic properties and reveal the reaction resistance changes. As can be seen in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S13</a> and Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S6</a> (Supporting Information), the charge transfer resistance (R<sub>ct</sub>) of the Fe<sub>x</sub>Co<sub>3-x</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs electrode were decreased and then increased. This is consistent with the results of in situ GEIS, where the reaction process is dominated by charge diffusion. It is shown that the electron transfer kinetics can be effectively improved with the iron lattice doping for the electrode material. When the Fe<sub>x</sub>Co<sub>3-x</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs electrode material is discharged, the R<sub>ct</sub> value of the Fe<sub>x</sub>Co<sub>3-x</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs electrode at 0.60&nbsp;V is lower (67.05&nbsp;Ω), showing the faster charge-transfer for Na<sup>+</sup> with the increase of capacity. <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub>&nbsp;decreased steadily due to the gradual decomposition of the SEI layer.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202412449-bib-0054" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202412449-bib-0054_R_d3386538e2216" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 54 - J. Mater. Sci. Technol.">54</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> This result can be confirmed from the galvanostatic intermittent titration technique (GITT) test curve (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S12</a>, Supporting Information). The Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion coefficient has a tendency to increase at 0.60&nbsp;V. When the Fe<sub>x</sub>Co<sub>3-x</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs electrode is charged, the R<sub>ct</sub> value of Fe<sub>x</sub>Co<sub>3-x</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs electrode at 1.20&nbsp;V is lower (29.84&nbsp;Ω), The higher Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion coefficient can be observed clearly. The in situ GEIS was conducted to explore the internal state associated with different potential levels, which is using infinite parallel resistance (R) and capacitance (C) to fit a complex system. Distribution of relaxation time (DRT) analysis was obtained based on in situ GEIS data. The τ value in DRT corresponds to electronic conductivity (10<sup>−6</sup>–10<sup>−5</sup>), particle and current collector contact (10<sup>−5</sup>–10<sup>−4</sup>), cathode electrolyte interface (10<sup>−4</sup>∼0.01), charge transfer in electrodes (0.01–10), and solid-state diffusion in electrodes (10–300), respectively.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202412449-bib-0055" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202412449-bib-0055_R_d3386538e2255" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 55 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.">55</a>, <a href="#smll202412449-bib-0056" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202412449-bib-0056_R_d3386538e2255" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 56 - Joule">56</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The DRT results of half batteries were decoupled by excluding the effect of the Na metal anode. The electronic resistance of the Fe<sub>x</sub>Co<sub>3-x</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs sample is consistently lower than that of the Co<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs sample throughout the entire charge–discharge process (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S14</a>, Supporting Information), which is consistent with the above analysis. This finding highlights the material's voltage-dependent resistance evolution and provides insight into the diffusion coefficient occurring during the electrochemical processes.</p>
            
            <p>To further study the cycle stability of the Fe<sub>x</sub>Co<sub>3-x</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs electrode,&nbsp;SEM and TEM were performed on the cycled electrodes (over 200 cycles) in the electrochemical process. A uniform SEI film was generated on the surface of Fe<sub>x</sub>Co<sub>3-x</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs, and the sea urchin-like morphology remained intact, as shown in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S16</a> (Supporting Information). The main component of the SEI layer is Na<sub>2</sub>O can be obtained from HRTEM (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S17</a>, Supporting Information) and elemental mapping (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S19</a>, Supporting Information).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202412449-bib-0001" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202412449-bib-0001_R_d3386538e2302" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 1 - Chem. Eng. J.">1</a>, <a href="#smll202412449-bib-0039" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202412449-bib-0039_R_d3386538e2302" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 39 - Nano Energy">39</a>, <a href="#smll202412449-bib-0054" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202412449-bib-0054_R_d3386538e2302" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 54 - J. Mater. Sci. Technol.">54</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Conversely, the Co<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs electrode was encapsulated by a thick SEI film (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S16</a>, Supporting Information), and a clear morphology of pulverized particles was observed. Additionally, TEM images of these electrodes after the 200th charge, Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S17</a> (Fe<sub>x</sub>Co<sub>3-x</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs, Supporting Information) and Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S18</a> (Co<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs, Supporting Information), reveal that a uniform SEI layer (2–3&nbsp;nm) was generated on the surface of the Fe<sub>x</sub>Co<sub>3-x</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs electrode and needle-like morphology is maintained after cycling (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S17c–d</a>, Supporting Information), consistent with elemental mapping observation (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S19a</a>, Supporting Information). Based on previous literature reports. Cobalt-based oxides with needle-like morphology have good cycling stability.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202412449-bib-0057" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202412449-bib-0057_R_d3386538e2345" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 57 - J. Power Sources">57</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The morphological evolution of Co<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4`</sub> electrodes before and after cycling is presented in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S18</a> (Supporting Information). After cycling, the initially pristine Co<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs undergo significant pulverization, resulting in the formation of smaller fragmented particles dispersed around larger agglomerates. The elemental mapping of Co<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs after cycling was displayed in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S19b</a> (Supporting Information). This structural degradation highlights the substantial mechanical stress and volume changes experienced during repeated charge/discharge cycles. In short, the high-rate performance mainly stems from multiple factors: i) the conversion reaction and surface pseudocapacitance provide high capacity; ii) the lower electronic resistance and higher diffusion coefficient during discharge/charge processes help to form the SEI film uniformly; iii) Enhancing of electrical conductivity reduces internal stress and partially mitigates volume expansion, contributing to improved structural stability during cycling.</p>
            </section>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smll202412449-sec-0060">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="smll202412449-sec-0060-title">2.4 Theoretical Calculations on the Effect of Iron Lattice Doping on Conductivity</h3>
            
            <p>The electron configurations of the 3d orbitals of cobalt and iron prominently dominate the conductivity of Fe<sub>x</sub>Co<sub>3-x</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs. We elucidated the underlying mechanisms that enhance the material's conductivity by analyzing the projected density of states (PDOS) of the cobalt and iron atoms within distinguished valance states. The bandgap values of the two models were calculated by constructing a unit of Co<sub>24</sub>O<sub>32</sub> (<b>Figure</b> <a href="#smll202412449-fig-0005">5a</a>) and replacing some iron atoms to form a new crystal unit (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202412449-fig-0005">5b</a>). The bandgaps of Fe<sub>2</sub>Co<sub>22</sub>O<sub>32</sub> (6%) decline from 1.57 to 1.38&nbsp;eV with the addition of two iron atoms in the unit cell (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202412449-fig-0005">5c,d</a>). Due to the presence of iron, the bandgap values for both the total and spin-up states narrow from 1.57 and 1.75&nbsp;eV to 1.29 and 1.53&nbsp;eV, respectively (Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S7</a>, Supporting Information). When iron atoms are doped, the spin-down electrons at the conduction band bottom shift slightly toward the Fermi energy level. As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202412449-fig-0005">5e</a>, the partial orbitals of tetrahedral coordinated divalent cobalt decrease in energy from ≈3.5&nbsp;eV to ≈2&nbsp;eV, which increases the density of states in the conduction band. This, in turn, allows more charge carriers to be available for conduction and enhances the material's electrical conductivity. A detailed simulation can be obtained in Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S7</a> (Supporting Information). Notably, when iron lattice doping between Co<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub>, the bandgap near the Fermi level is significantly reshaped, resulting in a higher density of electronic state (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202412449-fig-0005">5e</a>). Significantly, previous investigation results on iron lattice doping in Co<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub> will be presented in <b>Table</b> <a class="tableLink scrollableLink" title="Link to table" href="#smll202412449-tbl-0001">1</a>, as a supplementary reference for our findings. Bhisikar et&nbsp;al. investigated the distribution of iron composition at different iron lattice doping levels.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202412449-bib-0058" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202412449-bib-0058_R_d3386538e2435" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 58 - Inorg. Chem.">58</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> By summarizing the data, it was found that the doping concentration exceeds 8% (Co<sub>2.6</sub>Fe<sub>0.34</sub>O<sub>4.64</sub>), leading to Fe<sup>2+</sup> substitution of Co<sup>2+</sup> in the tetrahedral sites. This observation may account for the lower conductivity of 9% Fe doping compared to 6% Fe doping (Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1</a>, Supporting Information). As illustrated in Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S2</a> (Supporting Information), the incorporation of iron leads to the elongation of the Fe─O bond lengths within the octahedrally coordinated iron and cobalt atoms. This observation is consistent with experimental findings (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S2</a>, Supporting Information).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202412449-bib-0035" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202412449-bib-0035_R_d3386538e2460" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 35 - Nat. Commun.">35</a>, <a href="#smll202412449-bib-0059" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202412449-bib-0059_R_d3386538e2460" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 59 - Appl. Phys. A:Mater. Sci. Process.">59</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The doped iron atoms at the 8<i>a</i> site contribute to an increase in the volume of their tetrahedral coordination while simultaneously reducing the Co/Fe 16<i>d</i>-O bond lengths. This finding further confirms the enhanced electronic conductivity of Fe<sub>x</sub>Co<sub>3-x</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs compared to Co<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs. Iron lattice doping can reduce the bandgap between the conduction band and the valence band, enhancing electrical conductivity. This indicates that the presence of iron lattice doping sites is more favorable for the high-rate performance of sodium ions.</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="smll202412449-fig-0005"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/cbebb1ad-c233-4bcf-960a-319a97997b74/smll202412449-fig-0005-m.jpg"><picture>

         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smll202412449-sec-0070">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="smll202412449-sec-0070-title">2.5 Fe<sub>x</sub>Co<sub>3-x</sub>O<sub>4</sub> Versus PB Full Cell Study</h3>
            
            <p>The as-prepared Fe<sub>x</sub>Co<sub>3-x</sub>O<sub>4</sub> anode material was charged/discharged at a current density of 0.05&nbsp;A&nbsp;&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> for five cycles to form a stable SEI layer. The schematic illustration of the full cell is shown in <b>Figure</b> <a href="#smll202412449-fig-0006">6a</a>. For the experiment, the Prussian blue (PB) cathode was prepared as discussed in the Experimental Section by following the reported procedure.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202412449-bib-0061" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202412449-bib-0061_R_d3386538e2745" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 61 - J. Am. Chem. Soc.">61</a>, <a href="#smll202412449-bib-0062" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202412449-bib-0062_R_d3386538e2745" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 62 - Adv. Energy Mater.">62</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The constructed full cell was cycled in the 0.5–4.15&nbsp;V voltage range at a current rate of 0.5&nbsp;C (1&nbsp;C = 170&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>). Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202412449-fig-0006">6b</a> shows the charge–discharge profile of the full cells for the 1st, 10th, 20th, and 50th cycles, which shows similar charge–discharge reactions during each cycle. To test the feasibility of full batteries for real-world applications, we turned on the timer using a single coin cell, as shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202412449-fig-0006">6c</a>, which confirms the present technology for further developments in the field of transition metal oxides for future battery applications. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202412449-fig-0006">6d</a> shows the cycling behavior of the full cell up to ≈200 cycles, a discharge capacity of ≈110&nbsp;&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> was achieved after the 150th cycle by retaining ≈93% of the cell's initial capacity. Further, a considerable energy density of ≈255&nbsp;Wh&nbsp;kg<sup>−1</sup> at ≈3.65&nbsp;V region confirms the full cell's efficient energy conversion.</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="smll202412449-fig-0006"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/9c2c9da9-71a1-4ab4-9879-2fa79510b66e/smll202412449-fig-0006-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/9c2c9da9-71a1-4ab4-9879-2fa79510b66e/smll202412449-fig-0006-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/994ac92d-e79e-4c12-a44b-9006b6a79a7b/smll202412449-fig-0006-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/9c2c9da9-71a1-4ab4-9879-2fa79510b66e/smll202412449-fig-0006-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 6<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=smll202412449-fig-0006&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fsmll.202412449" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Electrochemical evaluations of the PB//NaClO<sub>4</sub>//Fe<sub>x</sub>Co<sub>3-x</sub>O<sub>4</sub> full cell. a) Schematic of the working process of SIBs, b) Detailed charge/discharge curves (0.5&nbsp;C, 1&nbsp;C = 170&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>), c) Application demonstration powered by the full cell, d) Cycling stability (0.5&nbsp;C).</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
         </section>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="smll202412449-sec-0080">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="smll202412449-sec-0080-title">3 Conclusion</h2>
         
         <p>Fe<sub>x</sub>Co<sub>3-x</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs were investigated as an anode electrode for SIBs in an ether-based electrolyte. Benefiting from the high diffusion contribution (8.64&nbsp;×&nbsp;10<sup>−12</sup> cm<sup>2</sup>&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup>), and the good electrical conductivity (11.64&nbsp;×&nbsp;10<sup>−3</sup>&nbsp;S&nbsp;cm<sup>−1</sup>), as-prepared Fe<sub>x</sub>Co<sub>3-x</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs endow to achieve a remarking rate capability of 402.9&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 3&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> and cycling stability barely without capacity fading 786.2&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 500 cycles at 0.5&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. We also used ex situ XRD and in situ GEIS methods to analyze the conversion reaction mechanism of sodium storage and proposed that iron lattice doping can increase the conductivity and decrease electronic resistance during discharge/charge processes of Fe<sub>x</sub>Co<sub>3-x</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs. The DFT calculation and UV–vis results confirmed that the Fe<sub>x</sub>Co<sub>3-x</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs electrode is more favorable for decreasing the bandgap (1.57 eV→1.38&nbsp;eV) with the lattice doping. Iron lattice doping can effectively increase the Co─O bond length, expanding the ion transport channels. In addition, the as-assembled Na-ion full cell displays a reversible capacity of 105&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> and good cycling durability ≈200 cycles. All these effects work together to obtain stable final high-rate performance. This work provides a promising anode material that may lead to the development of high-rate conversion materials with stable cycling for prospective energy storage applications.</p>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="smll202412449-sec-0090">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="smll202412449-sec-0090-title">4 Experimental Section</h2>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smll202412449-sec-0100">
            
            <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smll202412449-sec-0110">
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smll202412449-sec-0120">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="smll202412449-sec-0120-title"> Materials Synthesis</h4>
                  
                  <p>A co-precipitation doping synthesis method was designed to prepare Fe-doped Co<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub> nanoparticles (Fe<sub>x</sub>Co<sub>3-x</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs). In a typical process (6%-Fe<sub>x</sub>Co<sub>3-x</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs), 25&nbsp;m<span class="smallCaps">m</span> of Co(NO<sub>3</sub>)<sub>2</sub>·6H<sub>2</sub>O, 15&nbsp;m<span class="smallCaps">m</span> of Fe(NO<sub>3</sub>)<sub>3</sub>·9H<sub>2</sub>O, 46&nbsp;m<span class="smallCaps">m</span> of Urea and 68&nbsp;m<span class="smallCaps">m</span> of Ammonium fluoride (NH<sub>4</sub>F) were dissolved in DI water and stirred for 1&nbsp;h till the solution turned light pink. The solution was transferred into two 50&nbsp;mL Teflon-lined autoclaves, respectively, and then they were heated at 120&nbsp;°C for 12&nbsp;h. After that, they were cooled down to room temperature. Then, the processor products were collected by a centrifuge machine and washed with DI water and ethanol several times, followed by a vacuum drying process at 100&nbsp;°C for 12&nbsp;h. Finally, the processor was obtained by annealing the processor at 400&nbsp;°C for 2&nbsp;h under an Air atmosphere. When comparing the other samples (0%, 3%, 9%), all the conditions were kept the same, except for the difference in the content of Fe(NO)<sub>3</sub>.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smll202412449-sec-0130">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="smll202412449-sec-0130-title"> Materials Characterization</h4>
                  
                  <p>The crystalline structures of Fe<sub>x</sub>Co<sub>3-x</sub>O<sub>4</sub> NPs were identified with the X-ray diffractometer (XRD, SIEMENS D5000). The samples were scanned from 2θ = 10 ° to 90 ° at a rate of 0.02°&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup> in Bragg-Brentano geometry and a rate of 0.01°&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup> in Grazing-Incidence XRD with a copper (Cu) anode and Kα radiation. The samples were analyzed by XPS using a spectrometer (Thermos Scientific K-Alpha) with monochromatic Al-Kα radiation. Raman spectroscopy (WITec) with a He–Ne laser (532&nbsp;nm) was used to explore the vibration modes of Co─O bonds. The precise and accurate atomic ratio of Fe/Co was identified with the inductively coupled plasma-optical emission spectrometer (ICP-OES Agilent 5110). The morphologies and microstructures of samples were observed by an SEM (Hitachi S-4800) and an HRTEM (JEOL JEM-435 2100F). The corresponding elemental mapping was also investigated. The Mössbauer measurements were carried out at room temperature in transmission geometry with a custom-made miniaturized Mössbauer Spectrometer (MIMOS II) in self-production. A Co-57/Rh source was used and the measurements were recorded at 14.4&nbsp;keV. Data analysis was performed using the “Recoil” software (Rancourt and Ping, 2003). The velocity scale and isomer shift δ were calibrated with α-Fe (iron foil with 2.14% Fe-57, 20&nbsp;µm thick, 99.85% purity). Iron species were assigned by comparison of measured Mössbauer parameters to literature data. Resistivity measurements were made with a 4D four-point probe employing a Keithley 2400 programmable current source.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smll202412449-sec-0140">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="smll202412449-sec-0140-title"> Electrochemical Measurements</h4>
                  
                  <p>Working electrodes were fabricated by mixing the nanosheets assemblies, Super P, and carboxymethyl cellulose sodium with a weight ratio of 8:1:1. The mixture was uniformly coated (doctor-blade) on copper foils with a typical mass loading of around 1&nbsp;mg&nbsp;cm<sup>−2</sup>. It was then dried at 80&nbsp;°C under a vacuum for over 12&nbsp;h. Electrochemical measurements were performed using the configuration of coin cells CR2032 and the cells were assembled in an argon-filled glove box with oxygen and moisture concentrations below 0.1&nbsp;ppm. Na disc as the counter electrode was separated from the working electrode by a glass microfiber filter (Whatman, Grade GF/B). Electrolyte was 1&nbsp;<span class="smallCaps">m</span> sodium hexafluorophosphate in a 1, 2-dimethoxyethane (DME) solution was prepared in a nitrogen-filled glove box. Galvanostatic charge/discharge was carried out on a Land CT 2001A battery testing system (Land. China) at rates of 0.1–5&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at room temperature. Cyclic voltammetry (CV) and electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (EIS) were carried out by a VSP electrochemical workstation (Bio-Logic, France). To assemble Na-ion full cells, the Fe<sub>x</sub>Co<sub>3-x</sub>O<sub>4</sub> anode was pre-sodiation through five galvanostatic cycles at 50&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, which served to offset the initial capacity loss. Following this treatment, the prepared anode was combined with the PB cathode at a mass ratio of 1.2:1. The full cell's specific capacity was determined based on the mass of the PB cathode.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smll202412449-sec-0150">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="smll202412449-sec-0150-title"> Calculation Method</h4>
                  
                  <p>First-principles calculations based on DFT were carried out using the Vienna Ab initio Simulation Package (VASP).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202412449-bib-0063" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202412449-bib-0063_R_d3386538e2966" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 63 - Phys. Rev. B">63</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The PBE + U<sub>eff</sub> calculations were employed. The onsite Coulomb interaction U<sub>eff</sub> was 3.5&nbsp;eV for the Co ions and 4.3&nbsp;eV for the Fe ions.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202412449-bib-0064" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202412449-bib-0064_R_d3386538e2975" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 64 - Phys. Rev. B">64</a>, <a href="#smll202412449-bib-0065" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202412449-bib-0065_R_d3386538e2975" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 65 - Phys. Rev. B">65</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The initial magnetic moments were set. where 4&nbsp;µB for Co<sup>2+</sup>, 0&nbsp;µB for Co<sup>3+</sup>, 5.9&nbsp;µB for Fe<sup>3+</sup>, and 0.6&nbsp;µB for O<sup>2−</sup> throughout all calculations. A plane-wave cut-off energy of 700&nbsp;eV was applied and the convergence criteria for energy and forces were set to 1&nbsp;×&nbsp;10<sup>−8</sup>&nbsp;eV and 0.02&nbsp;eV&nbsp;Å<sup>−1</sup>, respectively. A Γ-centered 4&nbsp;×&nbsp;4&nbsp;×&nbsp;4 <i>k</i>-point mesh was used for the structural optimization. While the single-point calculations were performed using an increased 5&nbsp;×&nbsp;5&nbsp;×&nbsp;5 <i>k</i>-point mesh. Based on the tetrahedron method with Blöchl's corrections.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202412449-bib-0066" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202412449-bib-0066_R_d3386538e2998" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 66 - Phys. Rev. B">66</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The electronic band structures were computed along high-symmetry points in the Brillouin zone. Specifically, W (0.500, 0.250, 0.750), L (0.500, 0.500, 0.500), Γ (0.000, 0.000, 0.000), X (0.500, 0.000, 0.500), and K (0.375, 0.375, 0.750). The bandgap information was summarized by the VASPkit script.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202412449-bib-0067" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202412449-bib-0067_R_d3386538e3004" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 67 - Comput. Phys. Commun.">67</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Cobalt oxides crystalized in Spinel structure and Abhay reported that the unit cell can be doped with Fe ions at 16<i>d</i> Wyck site in trace amount.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202412449-bib-0058" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202412449-bib-0058_R_d3386538e3011" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 58 - Inorg. Chem.">58</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The initial model cells were constructed based on the real model of Co<sub>24-x</sub>Fe<sub>x</sub>O<sub>32</sub> (0 ≤ x ≤ 4). with increasing the randomly doping of iron atoms into the unit cell.</p>
                  </section>
               </section>
            </section>
         </section>
